1	# CLAUDE.md
2	
3	Project-specific guidance. Global rules (communication, git, credentials) live in `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` and are not repeated here. Design rationale lives in `playwright.md`; this file is the operational "what and how."
4	
5	## Project
6	
7	Web app that pulls a user's insurance policy documents from carrier portals via browser automation. Take-home for Infer (Forward Deployed Engineer), 48h deadline. Two carriers minimum, working end to end, hosted off the local machine, login to document render under ~8s.
8	
9	## Commands
10	
11	- Dev (watch): `npm run dev`
12	- Start: `npm start`
13	- Tests: `npm test` (Node test runner over `tests/**`)
14	- Typecheck: `npx tsc --noEmit`
15	
16	Server runs on http://localhost:3000 and serves the frontend at `/`. `start`/`dev` load
17	`.env` via `--env-file-if-exists`. Needs `BROWSERBASE_API_KEY`, `BROWSERBASE_PROJECT_ID`,
18	and for live Allstate `ALLSTATE_USER` / `ALLSTATE_PASSWORD` / `ALLSTATE_LOGIN_URL`.
19	Endpoints: `GET /carriers`, `POST /prepare`, `POST /login`, `POST /mfa`.
20

1	# Latency
2	
3	Graded metric: "MFA submission to document on screen" = `submitMfa` + `fetchDocuments`
4	(logged as `GRADED mfa-submit->docs`; for the no-MFA path, `GRADED login->docs`). Target ~8s.
5	Measure on prod (Fly `iad`, co-located with the Browserbase `us-east-1` session); local runs
6	slower for CDP-heavy steps but identical for browser->carrier work.
7	
8	## Where it stands
9	
10	- **Assurant: ~7.8s graded.** Meets the target. Single download (Confirmation of Coverage),
11	  Cloudflare edge in Newark (close to us-east-1).
12	- **Allstate (current `main`, full-API): ~5.3s doc stage** (local run, 3 docs). The UI-navigation
13	  version (~12s) is preserved on branch `allstate-ui-fallback`. Often skips MFA on a trusted
14	  device, so its graded span is mostly `fetchDocuments`.
15	
16	### Allstate full-API doc-stage breakdown (local run, MFA skipped, 3 docs)
17	| step | time | note |
18	|---|---|---|
19	| GetUserData + primer (parallel) | ~0.8s | the two independent GETs, fired together (was ~2.3s sequential) |
20	| GetPolicySpecificDocsList | ~0.2s | the doc list |
21	| GetUdpRetrieveDocument (parallel) | ~2.8s | one POST per doc, all overlapped; gated by the slowest single doc (server-side render variance, NOT size: a 9KB doc took 2.8s while a 1.24MB doc took 1.0s) |
22	| **full `fetchDocuments`** | **~5.3s** | local; prod (Fly `iad`) should be similar or faster for the API round trips |
23	
24	### Allstate doc-stage breakdown (prod, UI nav, 3 docs)
25	| step | time | note |
26	|---|---|---|
27	| nav-docs | ~6.4s | Policies dropdown -> Documents -> wait for table; `wait-table` alone ~3.3s (server fetch + render). Pure browser->carrier; co-location doesn't help. |
28	| trigger-downloads | ~4.2s | one popup + PDF download per doc, clicked sequentially; the downloads overlap (~0.4s), the clicks serialize |
29	| retrieve-list | ~0.3-2s | poll the Browserbase Downloads API |
30	| fetch-bytes | ~0.7s | pull each PDF's base64 (already parallel) |
31	
32	## Already done
33	- **Co-location** (Browserbase `us-east-1` + Fly `iad`). The big CDP-round-trip win.
34	- **Pre-warm** (`/prepare`): session create + login page load happen before the graded span.
35	- **Killed CSS animations** (addInitScript) so click "stability" waits don't burn time.
36	- **Parallelized `fetch-bytes`** (`collectDocuments`, Promise.all).
37	
38	## Tried and reverted
39	- Parallelizing the trigger-download clicks (`noWaitAfter` + popup listener): only the first
40	  click sped up; the rest re-serialize on the page settling after each popup. No net win.
41	
42	## The big win (now on `main`): full-API document fetch
43	Fetch documents straight from Allstate's JSON API from INSIDE the page (`session.fetchInPage`,
44	which runs `fetch()` via `page.evaluate`), skipping the UI nav, popups, and Browserbase download
45	storage entirely. **Doc stage ~5.3s.** The UI-navigation version is kept on branch
46	`allstate-ui-fallback` as a fallback (most human-like footprint, ~12s).
47	
48	Why in-page `fetch` and not `page.request`: `page.request` is a Node HTTP client, so it egresses
49	from our process (a Fly datacenter IP) with a Node/undici TLS fingerprint that does not match the
50	Chrome UA it sends. An in-page `fetch` rides the browser's residential-proxy IP, real Chrome TLS,
51	and cookies, so the API call looks like the app's own XHR. See the fingerprint notes below.
52	
53	Endpoints (host `myaccountrwd.allstate.com`), all authenticated by the session cookies:
54	1. `GET /api/secured/GetUserData` -> `policies[0].policyImage.number` (policy number).
55	2. `GET /api/secured/document/GetDocumentsForPolicies` -> **context primer**. Its own body is
56	   empty (`policyDocs:null`) but calling it scopes the session to the policy's documents. WITHOUT
57	   this call, step 3 returns an empty list. This was the whole blocker.
58	3. `POST /api/secured/document/GetPolicySpecificDocsList` body
59	   `{policyNumber, contentId:null, yearFilter}` -> `[{title, contentId, docYear

6	const LOGIN_URL = process.env.ASSURANT_LOGIN_URL ?? "https://manage.myassurantpolicy.com/app/login";
7	const STEP_TIMEOUT = 30_000;
8	
9	// Real Assurant (renters) portal automation. Auth is an embedded Okta widget:
10	// inputs #okta-signin-username / #okta-signin-password, submit #okta-signin-submit.
11	// MFA is an Okta SMS code into input[name=answer]. After login the account lands
12	// on /app/policy/selection; documents live on the server-rendered /Policy/Documents.
13	// Shared Browserbase plumbing (session + downloads) lives in BrowserbaseSession.
14	export class AssurantCarrier implements Carrier {
15	    readonly name = "assurant";
16	    private session?: BrowserbaseSession;
17	
18	    // Open the browser and load the Okta login form. No credentials needed, so
19	    // this can run ahead of login() to pre-warm while the user is still typing.
20	    async prepare(): Promise<void> {
21	        this.session = await BrowserbaseSession.open();
22	        const page = this.session.page;
23	        const tGoto = Date.now();
24	        await page.goto(LOGIN_URL, { waitUntil: "domcontentloaded" });
25	        console.log(`[timing] goto: ${Date.now() - tGoto}ms`);
26	        // the Okta widget renders client-side: wait for the username field
27	        const tForm = Date.now();
28	        await step(page, "assurant login-form", () =>
29	            page.locator("#okta-signin-username").waitFor({ timeout: STEP_TIMEOUT }),
30	        );
31	        console.log(`[timing] form-hydrate: ${Date.now() - tForm}ms`);
32	    }
33	
34	    async login(username: string, password: [REDACTED] Promise<{ mfaRequired: boolean }> {
35	        if (!this.session) await this.prepare(); // not pre-warmed: open + load the form now
36	        const page = requireSession(this.session).page;
37	
38	        const tSubmit = Date.now();
39	        await page.locator("#okta-signin-username").fill(username);
40	        await page.locator("#okta-signin-password").fill(password);
41	        await page.locator("#okta-signin-submit").click();
42	        console.log(`[timing]   form-actions: ${Date.now() - tSubmit}ms`);
43	
44	        // read the page: Okta code challenge, or straight into the account?
45	        const tNav = Date.now();
46	        let outcome: "mfa" | "dashboard";
47	        try {
48	            outcome = await Promise.race([
49	                page.locator('input[name="answer"]').waitFor({ timeout: STEP_TIMEOUT }).then(() => "mfa" as const),
50	                page.waitForURL(/\/app\/policy\//, { timeout: STEP_TIMEOUT }).then(() => "dashboard" as const),
51	            ]);
52	        } catch {
53	            // neither the code field nor the account appeared: almost always bad
54	            // credentials (Okta re-renders the form with an error). Surface a 401.
55	            throw new InvalidCredentialsError("login failed (check email and password)");
56	        }
57	        console.log(`[timing]   auth-nav: ${Date.now() - tNav}ms`);
58	        console.log(`[timing] submit+detect: ${Date.now() - tSubmit}ms`);
59	        if (outcome === "dashboard") return { mfaRequired: false }; // trusted device, no MFA
60	
61	        // MFA: tell Okta to send the SMS code; the code field is already rendered.
62	        await page
63	            .getByRole("link", { name: /send code/i })
64	            .or(page.getByRole("button", { name: /send code/i }))
65	            .first()
66	            .click();
67	        return { mfaRequired: true };
68	    }

1	# Known issues (deferred)
2	
3	Open items found in the chaos/QA pass that are not yet fixed. Revisit before final submit.
4	
5	## #2 No request/operation deadline: a hang wedges a session and leaks a browser
6	
7	Severity: high (resilience). Reasoned from code, not yet reproduced live.
8	
9	### What it is
10	The browser steps only have per-step timeouts (`STEP_TIMEOUT = 30s` on the Playwright
11	`waitFor`/`waitForURL` calls), and `BrowserbaseSession.open()`'s `chromium.connectOverCDP`
12	has **no timeout at all**. There is no overall per-request deadline and no Express server
13	timeout. So a single hang has nothing to stop it.
14	
15	### When it happens
16	- `connectOverCDP` hangs (Browserbase infra flap, network partition to the CDP
17	  websocket). The promise never resolves.
18	- Step timeouts stack: Allstate `fetchDocuments` worst case is
19	  `titles.waitFor (30s) + popup+download per doc (30s each) + retrieve-list (~22.5s)`,
20	  which can reach ~350s before any error surfaces.
21	
22	### Why it is bad
23	- `withLock` sets `session.inFlight`, and the reaper skips in-flight sessions on every
24	  sweep (`sessions.ts`), so a wedged session is **never reaped**.
25	- No Express request timeout, the HTTP connection hangs indefinitely; a client or
26	  upstream proxy may give up first.
27	- The Browserbase browser created at session open keeps billing and leaks until its
28	  own 1800s hard timeout.
29	- The only recovery is a process restart, which drops **all** other in-memory
30	  sessions (single instance, in-memory Map).
31	
32	### Where
33	- `src/browserbase.ts`: `open()` -> `connectOverCDP` (no timeout); `waitForDownloads`
34	  poll loop (15 x 1.5s).
35	- `src/sessions.ts`: reaper skips `session.inFlight`; `withLock`.
36	- `src/app.ts` / `src/server.ts`: no request timeout / no `server.requestTimeout`.
37	- carriers: `STEP_TIMEOUT = 30_000` per step.
38	
39	### Fix approach
40	1. Wrap `connectOverCDP` (and ideally each carrier operation) in a `Promise.race`
41	   against an explicit timeout that rejects with `CarrierTimeoutError`.
42	2. Add an overall per-operation deadline for `/login` and `/mfa` (e.g. 45-60s). On
43	   expiry, run `cleanup(sessionId)` (closes the browser, drops the session) and
44	   return `504`. This bounds tail latency and frees the leaked browser.
45	3. Wire `CarrierTimeoutError` (defined in `errors.ts`, mapped to 504 in `http.ts`,
46	   but currently never thrown) into the above. Also clears part of the dead-error
47	   taxonomy (QA #12).
48	4. Optional backstop: have the reaper also sweep in-flight sessions older than a hard
49	   max age, so a wedged op cannot live forever even if the deadline logic is missed.
50	
51	### Acceptance
52	A hung `connectOverCDP` returns a `504` within the deadline, the Browserbase session
53	is closed, and the session is removed from the Map. Worst-case `fetchDocuments` cannot
54	exceed the deadline.
55

assistant
Up to speed. Here's the picture on Assurant.

## What Assurant is
Renters insurance portal (`manage.myassurantpolicy.com`). Auth is an embedded **Okta** widget (`#okta-signin-username/password/submit`), MFA is an Okta SMS code into `input[name=answer]`. After login it lands on `/app/policy/selection`; the doc you pull is the **Confirmation of Coverage PDF** from the server-rendered policy documents view. Code is `src/carriers/assurant.ts`, behind the same `Carrier` interface as Allstate. Runs on Browserbase with a residential proxy.

## The latency problem
Graded span ("MFA submit to document on screen") is **~7.8s**. It technically meets the ~8s target, but barely. It's the slow carrier, sitting right against the wall, while Allstate was optimized down to ~5.3s.

The reason for the gap: Assurant is still on the **slow UI-navigation document path**, the same one Allstate was moved off of:

1. `nav-docs`: selection → click the `REN…` policy → snapshot → click "view policy documents" → wait for the "Policy Documents" heading.
2. `trigger-downloads`: click each "Download" control, each fires a real PDF download into **Browserbase download storage**. Clicks serialize.
3. `collectDocuments`: poll the Browserbase Downloads API, then pull the bytes back over CDP.

Allstate killed this whole path by calling the carrier's JSON document API in-page (`fetchInPage`), dropping ~12s → ~5.3s. **Assurant never got that treatment.**

## Why it wasn't optimized
The per-carrier anti-bot decision in `latency.md`: **Allstate runs Akamai**, which gates on the validated session cookie, so a fast `page.request` datacenter call still rides the legit session. **Assurant runs Cloudflare, which re-scores every individual request**, so a datacenter `page.request` is risky there. The safe fast option for Assurant would be an **in-page `fetch`** on the residential IP (same trick, residential instead of datacenter), but that hasn't been built for Assurant. It stays on UI-nav by default. Mitigating factor: only one small PDF, and Cloudflare edge is in Newark, close to us-east-1.

So the open lever is: replicate the in-page API fetch for Assurant's document endpoint to get it off the UI/download-storage path, staying on the residential IP to satisfy Cloudflare. There's no itemized Assurant timing table yet (only Allstate has one in `latency.md`), so step-level numbers would need a probe run first.

Want me to dig into the Assurant document endpoint (the `scripts/assurant-*` probes look like prior recon) and scope an in-page fetch path, or just stop at this briefing?

===== prod-drive.ts =====
// Drive a real Allstate flow against PROD (creds from .env in the request body;
// the browser + page.request run on the Fly machine). Prints only a safe summary
// (status + doc names/sizes); the base64 PDF bytes are written to a file, never
// to stdout. If MFA is required, drop the SMS code into scripts/prod-mfa.txt.
//   ! node --env-file=.env --import tsx scripts/prod-drive.ts
import { existsSync, readFileSync, rmSync, writeFileSync } from "node:fs";

const BASE = process.env.PROD_URL ?? "https://take-home-policy-puller.fly.dev";
const carrier = "allstate";

async function post(path: string, body: unknown): Promise<{ status: number; json: any }> {
  const t = Date.now();
  const r = await fetch(BASE + path, {
    method: "POST",
    headers: { "content-type": "application/json" },
    body: JSON.stringify(body),
  });
  const json = await r.json().catch(() => null);
  console.log(`[client] POST ${path} -> ${r.status} (${Date.now() - t}ms wall)`);
  return { status: r.status, json };
}

function summarize(documents: any[] | undefined): void {
  if (!documents) {
    console.log("no documents in response");
    return;
  }
  for (const d of documents) console.log(`  doc: ${d.name} | ${d.contentType} | base64 len=${(d.bytes || "").length}`);
  writeFileSync(
    "/tmp/prod-docs-meta.json",
    JSON.stringify(documents.map((d) => ({ name: d.name, contentType: d.contentType, len: (d.bytes || "").length })), null, 2),
  );
}

const prep = await post("/prepare", { carrier });
const warmId = prep.json?.warmId;
console.log("prepare:", prep.status, warmId ? "warmId ok" : JSON.stringify(prep.json));

const login = await post("/login", {
  carrier,
  username: process.env.ALLSTATE_USER,
  password: [REDACTED],
  warmId,
});
console.log("login:", login.status, login.json?.status ?? JSON.stringify(login.json));

let documents = login.json?.documents;
if (login.json?.status === "mfa_needed") {
  const sessionId = login.json.sessionId;
  console.log(">>> MFA needed. Drop the SMS code into scripts/prod-mfa.txt");
  let code = "";
  for (let i = 0; i < 150; i++) {
    if (existsSync("scripts/prod-mfa.txt")) {
      code = readFileSync("scripts/prod-mfa.txt", "utf8").trim();
      rmSync("scripts/prod-mfa.txt");
      break;
    }
    await new Promise((r) => setTimeout(r, 2000));
  }
  if (!code) {
    console.log("no code, aborting");
    process.exit(1);
  }
  const mfa = await post("/mfa", { sessionId, code });
  console.log("mfa:", mfa.status, mfa.json?.status ?? JSON.stringify(mfa.json));
  documents = mfa.json?.documents;
}

summarize(documents);
console.log("done.");
process.exit(0);

I've got full ground truth now. Key facts the agents must start from:

- **Assurant graded (MFA-submit → docs) ≈ 7.8s**, doc stage ≈ 7s. Barely under the 8s wall. Allstate is ≈5.3s.
- **Critical learning from the latest commit (`cd1f551`):** the in-page `fetch` of doc URLs was already tried and **reverted** — it ran ~9.6s because base64-over-CDP on real PDFs is slow. The download-to-storage path (~7s doc stage) won. So "just do what Allstate did" is a known dead end for Assurant.
- The download path = `nav-docs` (selection→snapshot→view-docs→wait-heading) → serial `trigger-downloads` clicks → `retrieve-list` (poll `waitForDownloads`, **15×1.5s coarse granularity**) → parallel `fetch-bytes`.
- Anti-bot constraint: Assurant = Cloudflare, **re-scores every request**, so the datacenter `page.request` fast path Allstate uses is off-limits.

Now I'll orchestrate the agents as a workflow: parallel probe (performance + pentest + backend), parallel web research, then synthesis, then an adversarial verify pass that checks every recommendation against the known-failed attempts.

Write  {"file_path":"/home/dan/Projects/Take_Home/scripts/prod-drive-assurant.ts","content":"// Drive the real Assurant flow against PROD end to end (browser + scrape run on\n// the Fly machine / Browserbase; creds go in the request body from .env). Prints\n// only a safe summary (status + doc names/sizes); base64 PDF bytes are written to\n// a file, never to stdout. The authoritative GRADED + per-step budget is in the\n// Fly server logs ([timing] lines); this client view adds TTFB so we can separate\n// server graded time from the base64 response transfer back to the client.\n// MFA: drop the SMS code into scripts/assurant-mfa.txt.\n//   ! node --env-file=.env --import tsx scripts/prod-drive-assurant.ts\nimport { existsSync, readFileSync, rmSync, writeFileSync } from \"node:fs\";\n\nconst BASE = process.env.PROD_URL ?? \"https://take-home-policy-puller.fly.dev\";\nconst carrier = \"assurant\";\n\n// POST that separates time-to-first-byte (≈ server done + 1 network leg) from the\n// full body read (adds the base64 PDF transfer, which is NOT part of the graded span).\nasync function post(path: string, body: unknown): Promise<{ status: number; json: any; ttfbMs: number; fullMs: number }> {\n  const t = Date.now();\n  const r = await fetch(BASE + path, {\n    method: \"POST\",\n    headers: { \"content-type\": \"application/json\" },\n    body: JSON.stringify(body),\n  });\n  const ttfbMs = Date.now() - t; // fetch resolves on response headers\n  const json = await r.json().catch(() => null);\n  const fullMs = Date.now() - t; // after the full body (base64 PDFs) is read\n  console.log(`[client] POST ${path} -> ${r.status}  ttfb=${ttfbMs}ms  full=${fullMs}ms`);\n  return { status: r.status, json, ttfbMs, fullMs };\n}\n\nfunction summarize(documents: any[] | undefined): void {\n  if (!documents) return console.log(\"no documents in response\");\n  for (const d of documents) console.log(`  doc: ${d.name} | ${d.contentType} | base64 len=${(d.bytes || \"\").length}`);\n  writeFileSync(\n    \"/tmp/prod-assurant-docs-meta.json\",\n    JSON.stringify(documents.map((d) => ({ name: d.name, contentType: d.contentType, len: (d.bytes || \"\").length })), null, 2),\n  );\n}\n\nconst tPrep = Date.now();\nconst prep = await post(\"/prepare\", { carrier });\nconst warmId = prep.json?.warmId;\nconsole.log(`prepare: ${prep.status} ${warmId ? \"warmId ok\" : JSON.stringify(prep.json)}  (${Date.now() - tPrep}ms, off the graded clock)`);\n\nconst login = await post(\"/login\", {\n  carrier,\n  username: process.env.ASSURANT_USER,\n  password: [REDACTED],\n  warmId,\n});\nconsole.log(\"login:\", login.status, login.json?.status ?? JSON.stringify(login.json));\n\nlet documents = login.json?.documents;\nlet gradedTtfb: number | undefined;\nlet gradedFull: number | undefined;\n\nif (login.json?.status === \"mfa_needed\") {\n  const sessionId = login.json.sessionId;\n  console.log(\">>> MFA needed. SMS sent. Drop the code into scripts/assurant-mfa.txt\");\n  let code = \"\";\n  for (let i = 0; i < 150; i++) {\n    if (existsSync(\"scripts/assurant-mfa.txt\")) {\n      code = readFileSync(\"scripts/assurant-mfa.txt\", \"utf8\").trim();\n      rmSync(\"scripts/assurant-mfa.txt\");\n      break;\n    }\n    await new Promise((r) => setTimeout(r, 2000));\n  }\n  if (!code) {\n    console.log(\"no code received in 5 min, aborting\");\n    process.exit(1);\n  }\n  const mfa = await post(\"/mfa\", { sessionId, code });\n  console.log(\"mfa:\", mfa.status, mfa.json?.status ?? JSON.stringify(mfa.json));\n  documents = mfa.json?.documents;\n  gradedTtfb = mfa.ttfbMs;\n  gradedFull = mfa.fullMs;\n} else if (login.json?.status === \"done\") {\n  // trusted device, no MFA: the graded span was login->docs\n  gradedTtfb = login.ttfbMs;\n  gradedFull = login.fullMs;\n}\n\nsummarize(documents);\nif (gradedTtfb !== undefined) {\n  console.log(`\\n===== CLIENT-SIDE GRADED PROXY =====`);\n  console.log(`  ttfb (≈ server graded + 1 network leg):   ${gradedTtfb}ms`);\n  console.log(`  full (ttfb + base64 PDF transfer to me):  ${gradedFull}ms`);\n  console.log(`  >>> authoritative GRADED is the Fly log line \"[timing] GRADED ...\".`);\n}\nconsole.log(\"done.\");\nprocess.exit(0);\n"}

Measured. Real prod end-to-end works — but the number is the story.

## Real prod Assurant: graded = 14.4s (not the documented ~7.8s)

Live run just now, full chain on prod (`/prepare` → `/login` → SMS MFA → `/mfa`), browser on Browserbase us-east-1 + Fly iad. Returned 1 PDF (ConfirmationOfCoverage, 58 KB). Server-authoritative `[timing]` from Fly logs:

| Step | Time | % | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `submitMfa` (Okta verify → `/app/policy`) | ~2,635 ms | 18% | derived: graded − doc steps. Full SPA nav through Cloudflare |
| `nav-docs` | 5,514 ms | 38% | selection→snapshot→view-docs→wait heading. Pure browser→carrier render, co-location doesn't help |
| `trigger-downloads` | 3,554 ms | 25% | click + `waitForEvent('download')`, serial |
| `retrieve-list` | 2,211 ms | 15% | poll Browserbase Downloads API (1,500 ms granularity) |
| `fetch-bytes` | 512 ms | 4% | parallel binary GET from BB storage |
| **GRADED mfa-submit→docs** | **14,426 ms** | | client TTFB corroborates: 14,469 ms |

Pre-warm (`/prepare`, off the graded clock): ~4.8s — session-create 511ms + cdp-connect 922ms + goto 2,493ms + form-hydrate 625ms. Fine where it is.

## Two things this changes

1. **The ~7.8s baseline in `latency.md`/`CLAUDE.md` is wrong for prod.** Real download-path graded is **14.4s — ~6.4s over the 8s target**, not under it. The "7.8s" was never reproduced here. So Assurant currently *fails* the spec gate on prod.

2. **The Fly log also caught the reverted in-page attempt in the wild:** an earlier run shows `api-docs (in-page): 9,612ms` → `GRADED: 22,403ms`. Confirms the commit message empirically — in-page base64 is far worse. The download path is the better of two bad options.

The dominant costs are `nav-docs` (5.5s) and `trigger-downloads` (3.5s), both browser↔carrier render gated by Cloudflare, plus a soft 2.2s in the coarse poll loop.

**Caveat:** single MFA run, so one sample. Historical log lines corroborate the magnitude (nav-docs ranged 4.5–7.8s across runs), so 14.4s is representative, not a fluke — but the per-step numbers carry render variance.

62	      // login is fast on submit. Kicked off on page load AND on carrier change.
63	      // prepare() is slow (~11s: Allstate's SPA hydrates), so we keep the in-flight
64	      // promise in `preparing` and have login() await it — otherwise a user who
65	      // submits before prepare returns sends warmId:null and /login cold-starts a
66	      // SECOND full prepare (~22s). Awaiting guarantees the warm session is reused.
67	      function prepare() {
68	        warmId = null;
69	        const carrier = $("carrier").value;
70	        if (!carrier) {
71	          preparing = null;
72	          return;
73	        }
74	        // surface the warm-up so the user has a reason not to submit into a cold
75	        // session; cleared to "Ready" once the session is warm.
76	        show("Preparing a secure session...");
77	        preparing = (async () => {
78	          try {
79	            const res = await fetch("/prepare", {
80	              method: "POST",
81	              headers: { "content-type": "application/json" },
82	              body: JSON.stringify({ carrier }),
83	            });
84	            const data = await res.json();
85	            if (res.ok) {
86	              warmId = data.warmId;
87	              show("Ready. Enter your credentials.");
88	            }
89	          } catch {
90	            /* pre-warm is best-effort; login still works (just slower) without it */
91	          }
92	        })();
93	      }

assistant
Already done, actually. The frontend warms on page load today:

- `loadCarriers()` runs on load, defaults to the first real carrier, and calls `prepare()` immediately (`public/index.html:55`).
- `/prepare` opens the Browserbase session, loads the Okta login page, and hydrates the form. From the prod run that is session-create 0.5s + cdp-connect 0.9s + goto 2.5s + form-hydrate 0.6s, about **4.5s, all off the graded clock**.
- `login()` awaits the in-flight `preparing` promise (`index.html:124`), so even a fast submit reuses the warm session instead of cold-starting a second prepare.

So the pre-login path is genuinely not cold. That part of your instinct is already shipped.

The catch is *what* is left to warm. The 14.4s graded span is `submitMfa` + `nav-docs` + downloads, and every one of those is **post-authentication and post-MFA**. There is no logged-in session to navigate the policy/snapshot/documents pages with until the human passes MFA, so none of it can be pre-warmed on page load. You can warm the door, not the rooms behind the lock.

The only warmable surface left is the **human MFA pause** (between `/login` returning `mfa_needed` and the user submitting the code). That window is free wall-clock time, not graded. During it the session sits on the Okta challenge, still unauthenticated for the app, so we still cannot fetch documents. The most we could do is warm the network connection (TLS/HTTP2 + Cloudflare clearance) to the documents host so the post-MFA nav is not Cloudflare's first sight of us. Two reasons I would rank it low:
1. The cookies and a Cloudflare clearance are already established from the login navigation on the same origin, so the connection is mostly warm anyway.
2. Assurant is Cloudflare, which re-scores every request. Firing speculative requests during the pause adds bot signal for little time saved. That is the exact constraint pinning the rest of this work.

A session pool (pre-create Browserbase browsers before the user even picks a carrier) would shave the ~0.5s session-create, but that is off-clock too, so it improves the pre-login wait, not the graded number.

Bottom line: cold start is already eliminated by the on-load `/prepare`. The 14.4s is warm-path, auth-gated work, so warming is not the lever. The graded number only moves by making the post-MFA `nav-docs` and download steps themselves faster, which is exactly what the running synthesis is targeting. I'll fold this "warming is maxed, pause-warm is low-value" conclusion into the writeup when the workflow lands.

# Writing git commit messages

Default: one short subject line. State exactly what was done. Nothing else.

Add a body only when the WHY is non-obvious from the diff, and keep it to 1 or 2 terse lines. KISS.

Source: https://cbea.ms/git-commit/

## The seven rules

1. Separate subject from body with a blank line.
2. Limit subject to 50 chars (72 is the hard ceiling).
3. Capitalize the subject (override below for repo-specific prefix style).
4. No period at the end of the subject.
5. Imperative mood. "Fix bug" not "Fixed bug" or "Fixes bug".
6. Wrap the body at 72 chars.
7. Body explains what and why, not how. The diff already shows how.

## The subject-line test

A good subject completes the sentence: "If applied, this commit will ___."

Passes: "Refactor X module". Fails: "Fixed bug", "Sweeping changes", "More fixes".

## Style rules (hard)

- No em dashes or en dashes anywhere. Use periods, commas, or restructure.
- No semicolons. Comma or period.
- No emojis.
- No `Co-Authored-By:` lines.
- No `Generated with Claude Code` or similar footers.
- Never list Claude as author. Check `git config user.name` and `user.email` before committing.
- Don't repeat the prefix in the description. `fix: Fix X` is redundant.

## Plain verbs to default to

fix, add, remove, rename, move, extract, drop, revert, bump, pin, unpin, wire up, clean up, stub out, expose, hide, replace, restore, ignore, gate, skip.

## Banned AI-tell words

comprehensive, enhance, streamline, robust, leverage, utilize, ensure, rectify, "this commit introduces", "implement comprehensive", "this change adds support for".

If any appear in a draft, rewrite the subject.

## Repo-specific overrides

If the repo's `AGENTS.md` or `CONTRIBUTING.md` defines a style, follow that instead of rule 3:

- **Peeky style**: lowercase area prefix, colon, terse description. Examples: `tuning: zero post-release grace`, `demos: move examples/ to demos/`, `deny: ignore RUSTSEC-2026-0009`.
- **Conventional Commits style**: `feat(scope): ...`, `fix(scope): ...`, `chore(scope): ...` (used in Node/Angular/Vercel ecosystems).

The other six rules still apply.

## When a body is justified

- The change is non-obvious from the diff (workaround, perf trick, surprising ordering).
- The why needs context outside this file (incident ID, advisory, upstream bug).
- Closing a tracked issue: include `closes #N` (repeat per issue, a shared keyword only closes the first).

If the diff explains itself, write no body. One line is enough.

## Examples

Good, single-line:

```
tuning: zero post-release grace
demos: move examples/ to demos/
deny: ignore RUSTSEC-2026-0009 (time, blocked by tract pin)
fix rustfmt on screenshot guard in find_action
```

Good, with justified body:

```
routelet: cap the opt-in log and document data handling

Bound routelet_log.jsonl to its last 5000 lines. Storage cap, not a
privacy fix. Logging is already opt-in and redacted.
```

Bad (rewrite these):

```
Add comprehensive support for enhanced cursor positioning
```
Rewrite as: `cursor: snap to nearest target on partial match`.

```
This commit introduces a robust solution for the STT cutoff issue
```
Rewrite as: `stt: add 200ms post-release grace to capture trailing audio`.

## Workflow

1. Stage exact paths. Never `git add -A` or `git add .`.
2. `git status` to confirm only your changes are staged.
3. Draft the subject. Apply the "If applied" test.
4. Body only if justified above.
5. `git commit -m "..."` with HEREDOC for multi-line.
6. Never push unless asked.

## Red flags

- Subject describes how, not what or why.
- Subject would still make sense if pasted into a different PR. Too vague.
- Body restates the diff line by line.
- Two unrelated changes in one commit. Split them.
- Any banned word above.

## When to consult the master reference

For deeper coverage, see the `writing` skill (manual invoke: `/writing`) which compiles all writing rules, or `d

   depends=None. Independent, ships standalone, hardens the fallback. Requires redeploy.

R4 [risk=low conf=medium antibot=true] Overlap fetch-bytes with the poll tail and start the poll concurrently with the download click (multi-doc / fallback only)
   save=0 on single-COC path; 200-500 only if 2+ docs are fetched via fallback
   files=src/browserbase.ts, src/carriers/assurant.ts
   depends=Only meaningful for multi-doc fallback. Bundle with R3. Requires redeploy.

R5 [risk=low conf=high antibot=true] Add ?createdAfter=<t0-2s> filter to the downloads poll for retry-safe early resolution
   save=0 direct (correctness enabler that makes R3's early ticks trustworthy)
   files=src/browserbase.ts, src/carriers/assurant.ts
   depends=Pairs with R3. Requires redeploy.

=== WHAT NOT TO TRY ===
 - In-page fetch of ALL Assurant documents (scrape every documentToken anchor + fetch the large table PDFs as base64-over-CDP): measured ~9.6s for the 'api-docs' step / ~22.4s graded in the wild and reverted in cd1f551. The CDP base64 channel is slow for large PDF payloads. NOTE this does NOT condemn POI-ONLY (58KB) fetch: the 9.6s number also included full nav-docs + table-render wait + the big-PDF fetches; R1 isolates just the small COC. Do not conflate the two.
 - Parallelizing the trigger-download CLICKS (noWaitAfter + parallel waitForEvent): tried on Allstate and reverted. Only the first click speeds up; the rest re-serialize as the page settles after each popup/download. Same single-page DOM mechanics on Assurant. Moot once R1 removes clicks entirely.
 - page.request / any Node datacenter HTTP client for Assurant doc bytes: Cloudflare re-scores EVERY request by IP + JA3/JA4 TLS. A Fly datacenter IP + Node/undici TLS on a Chrome UA is a per-request tell. (Allstate can do this because Akamai gates on the validated session COOKIE, not per-request IP; Assurant cannot.) Keep all Assurant carrier traffic in-page (residential proxy + Chrome TLS).
 - Browserbase Verified mode for Assurant: already removed. Cloudflare does not need it and the heavier fingerprint negotiation slowed the multi-step UI nav. Do not re-add.
 - JS navigator overrides (hardwareConcurrency, deviceMemory defineProperty, etc.): banned. A non-[native code] getter is itself a detectable own-property accessor on a real profile, and nothing in the measured attack surface reads these. Leave the fingerprint native.
 - Direct page.goto to the documents URL: lands back on /selection and strips the same-origin

=== ADVERSARIAL VERDICTS ===
[rank 1] Capture the FULL REN at submitMfa and fetch ONLY the COC via in-page POI, skipping nav-docs + trigger-downloads + poll entirely
   verdict=RISKY action=keep-with-caveat conflicts_known_failure=false adj_save=Probability-weighted ~3000-5000 ms expected (graded ~14.4s -> ~9-11s), NOT the claimed 9000-11000 ms. The full ~9-11s saving only materializes in the ~40-50% case where the snapshot-URL REN happens to be the POI-accepted full form. In the more-likely failure case it saves ~0 and ADDS a wasted in-page POI round-trip (~1-2s) before falling back to the existing path.
   The mechanism is sound where it differs from the reverted path, but the load-bearing assumption is contradicted by existing recon, so the headline savings are unlikely to land.

WHAT IS SOUND: The proposal correctly distinguishes itself from the reverted 9.6s/22.4s in-page path (commit 90482ec). That path ran FULL nav-docs, waited for the table, scraped ALL documentToken anchors, and base64'd the LARGE table PDFs over CDP. A POI-only fetch of the ConfirmationOfCoverage PDF is 58KB decoded (confirmed by the prod run), so base64-over-CDP for it is cheap (~0.5-1s, in line with the measured 512ms fetch-bytes). It does NOT re-introduce the known-failed big-PDF-over-CDP cost. It is also anti-bot safe: it uses fetchInPage (residential IP + Chrome TLS + cookies), not page.request, so it does not repeat the datacenter-client mistake on Cloudflare. And skipping the view-policy-documents click + Policy Documents heading wait legitimately removes the 5.5s nav-docs render and the 3.5s serial trigger-downloads + 2.2s poll IF the byte channel works without that nav.

WHY IT IS RISKY (the refutation): The proposal's own declared BLOCKING UNKNOWN is the entire ballgame, and the existing evidence points AGAINST it. Commit 90482ec (the probe-derived result) states plainly: 'build the POI URL from the FULL policy number in a doc href (the selection-list shows a SHORTER form the POI endpoint REJECTS).' The probe scripts/assurant-docpage-probe.ts fed the selection-text REN (/REN\d+/) straight into the exact POI URL this proposal builds, and that was the rejected case; only the full REN scraped from a documentToken href worked. The snapshot URL the proposal reads with page.url() is reached by clicking that same selection-list REN element, so the snapshot-path REN is almost certainly the same short form that POI rejects, not the full form. If so, R1 never succeeds and silently falls back to R2 (the current path) on every run, yielding ZERO net savings plus a wasted ~1-2s POI round-trip and a required redeploy off cd1f551.

SECONDARY RISK: even granting the REN works, the proposal is vague about the selection->snapshot navigation. POI/COC is served against an ACTIVE policy (the current code clicks selection -> waits for /snapshot specifically to set the policy active server-side). If fetchDocuments fires POI while still on /selection, it likely 404s. The rewrite must retain the selection->snapshot click (cheap, no view-docs/heading wait) before the POI fetch; the proposal only explicitly skips the view-docs click, which is fine, but it should not also skip selection->snapshot. The savings claim is computed against collapsing nav-docs(5.5)+trigger(3.5)+poll(2.2)+bytes(0.5); a retained selection->snapshot adds back a small render but is far cheaper than the full nav-docs.

NET: This is the single highest-upside lever in the set and it is genuinely a different cost class from the reverted path, but its success is gated on one unverified URL-format fact that prior recon suggests is false. It must NOT ship as a blind redeploy. It needs exactly the one read-only live MFA run the proposal itself names: log page.url() at submitMfa and the documentToken href REN, and confirm they are byte-identical AND that POI accepts the URL-form REN. Ship only after that confirms; otherwise it is a no-op-with-overhead.

## The plan, against the real 14.4s budget

| Step | Now | After the fix | Lever |
|---|---|---|---|
| `submitMfa` (Okta+Cloudflare auth nav) | 2,635 ms | 2,635 ms | none possible (hard floor) |
| `nav-docs` | 5,514 ms | **0 or ~5,514** | R1 skips it — *if* feasible |
| `trigger-downloads` | 3,554 ms | **0** | R1 eliminates clicks |
| `retrieve-list` (poll) | 2,211 ms | 0 (R1) or ~600 (R3) | R1 removes / R3 tightens |
| `fetch-bytes` | 512 ms | ~600–1,400 | single 58 KB COC over CDP |
| **GRADED** | **14,426** | **~3.7–4.8s (R1 works)** or **~9.5–10s (R1 blocked)** | |

## The one lever that matters — and its blocker

**R1: capture the full policy number (REN) right after MFA, then fetch only the Confirmation of Coverage PDF directly via the in-page POI endpoint, skipping nav-docs + download clicks + poll entirely.** This is genuinely *not* the reverted in-page path (that one fetched the big table PDFs over CDP; this fetches one 58 KB doc, which is cheap). Anti-bot safe — it uses `fetchInPage` (residential IP + Chrome TLS), not the datacenter client.

**Adversarial verdict: RISKY / keep-with-caveat.** The whole thing hinges on one unverified fact, and prior recon points *against* it: per commit `90482ec` and the existing probes, the selection/snapshot REN is a **short form the POI endpoint rejects** — the full REN was only ever recovered from a documents-table anchor, which requires nav-docs to render. If that holds, R1 silently falls back and saves ~0 (probability-weighted expected save ~3–5s, not the headline 9–11s). And even the fallback (skip downloads, keep nav-docs) lands at **~9.5–10s, still over 8s**, because nav-docs (5.5s) is Cloudflare-gated render that nothing but *avoidance* can fix.

## The honest bottom line
- **There is no safe blind-deploy path to sub-8s.** Everything pivots on whether the full REN is available *before* the documents table renders.
- The cheap, safe, standalone win is **R3** (poll backoff): SOUND, ~0.7–1s, low-risk, but cannot get 14.4s → 8s alone. R4/R5 are ~0 on the single-doc path (verifiers said drop R4's "concurrent poll" half; R5 guards a failure mode that isn't even reachable today).

So the decisive next step is **recon, not code, and it needs no redeploy**: one read-only live run that logs the snapshot URL's REN, the table-anchor REN, and whether POI accepts the snapshot-form REN. That single fact decides whether Assurant can hit ~4.5s or is stuck near ~9.5s. Let me confirm what the existing probes already settled before asking you for another MFA.

assistant
Conclusive. The recon settles R1 and reshapes the whole problem:

## Recon result (live, this session)

| REN source | value | POI result |
|---|---|---|
| post-MFA URL (`/app/policy/selection`) | **no REN** | — |
| snapshot URL (`/app/policy/snapshot`) | **no REN** | — |
| selection page text | `REN[REDACTED]` (short) | `200` but **`text/html`** → rejected, 1441ms |
| documents-table anchor | `REN[REDACTED]` (full) | **`200 application/pdf` 58 KB, 3057ms** ✓ |

So, definitively:
- **The full REN is in no URL.** It only appears on the documents-table anchor, which requires `nav-docs` to render.
- **POI accepts only the full REN.** The short form returns an HTML error page.
- **POI itself costs ~3.0s** (carrier-side PDF generation; the 58 KB transfer is trivial).

## What that does to the budget
R1 and R2's optimistic paths are dead. If we still must render `nav-docs` (5.5s) just to read the full REN, then swap the download tail for POI:
`submitMfa 2.6 + nav-docs 5.5 + POI 3.0 ≈ **11.1s**` — saves ~3.3s but **still over 8s**. POI being 3.0s (not the assumed 1-2s) makes it worse than the verifier's estimate.

## The one remaining path to sub-8s
Get the full REN **without rendering the documents table** — a cheap in-page API call right after MFA, exactly like Allstate's `GetUserData`. The selection page shows `REN[REDACTED]` but the API backing it almost certainly knows the full `REN[REDACTED]`. If that value is available from a selection-phase API, the path becomes:
`submitMfa 2.6 + REN-from-API ~0.5-1 + POI 3.0 ≈ **~6.1-6.6s**` → under 8s with margin.

That is the decisive unknown, and it needs **one more MFA run** (read-only, no redeploy): capture every Assurant `/api` response from login onward, then find the earliest one carrying the full REN. This is the last recon before implementation — it gives a measured go/no-go.

Let me write that capture probe.

The recon nearly nailed it, and revealed the smoking gun:

## What the capture found

| Phase | Time post-MFA | Endpoint |
|---|---|---|
| submitMfa | 0ms | `/api/SetOktaUserIdAndToken` |
| selection | 247ms | `/api/ResetBlitzPolicyView` |
| **selection** | **1802ms** | **`/api/PolicyId`** ← fires early, before docs |
| docs | 6957ms | `/api/Policies/REN[REDACTED]/Documents?lob=RI` |

The full REN (`REN[REDACTED]`) is already in the app's hands by the time it builds the Documents URL — and the only thing that could have given it that is **`/api/PolicyId`**, which fires at **1.8s during selection, well before nav-docs**. 

My probe reported "none of the bodies contained the full REN" only because it filtered to JSON/text content-types and **`/api/PolicyId` returned a blank content-type, so its body was never read.** That endpoint is the prime suspect for the full REN, and it's exactly the cheap, early call we need.

## The path to sub-8s
`submitMfa 2.6 + /api/PolicyId ~0.5 + POI 3.0 ≈ **~6.1s**`, under 8s with margin — *if* `PolicyId` yields the full REN.

Rather than burn another MFA on pure recon, I'll collapse the last unknown into the implementation: build the fast path with **tolerant REN parsing + a safe fallback to the existing download path**, plus a validation harness that dumps `PolicyId`'s body and measures the new graded span. One live run then both confirms `PolicyId`'s shape and validates the fix.

Per ultracode, I'll write and adversarially review the implementation via a workflow (anti-bot + correctness) before the live test, writing to scratch files so the working `assurant.ts` isn't touched until vetted.

  - Harness nit: prototype monkey-patch of fetchInPage moved inside the try with a 'patched' guard; finally restores only if patched, so a setup throw cannot leave the prototype patched globally
  - Type-safety (beyond reviews): replaced the captured-let policyIdBodyCapture with a holder object { body: string | null } so closure mutation is visible to the type checker; without it tsc narrowed the read site to 'never'

residual_risks:
  - App-specific POI request headers (x-requested-with, auth bearer/okta token, accept-language) are NOT mirrored, only accept+referer are sent. Reviewer marked this minor/defer-if-minimal-works. Confirm on the live run that the minimal-header POI returns the PDF cleanly; if not, capture the genuine app XHR headers in devtools and mirror them.
  - networkidle waits are best-effort with .catch(()=>{}) and a 30s timeout; a perpetually-busy SPA may never go fully idle, in which case the wait burns up to the full timeout before proceeding. Live timing will confirm the settle adds the expected ~1-2s and not a stall. If it stalls, swap to a bounded waitForURL/short fixed wait.

4	import { BrowserbaseSession, step, requireSession, jitter } from "../browserbase.js";
5	
6	const LOGIN_URL = process.env.ASSURANT_LOGIN_URL ?? "https://manage.myassurantpolicy.com/app/login";
7	// Derive the API origin from the login URL so the fast-path API calls track the
8	// same host as the rest of the carrier (e.g. a staging ASSURANT_LOGIN_URL points
9	// both the page nav AND the in-page API fetches at the same place). Falls back to
10	// prod if the env value is somehow unparseable.
11	const ORIGIN = (() => {
12	    try {
13	        return new URL(LOGIN_URL).origin;
14	    } catch {
15	        return "https://manage.myassurantpolicy.com";
16	    }
17	})();
18	const STEP_TIMEOUT = 30_000;
19	
20	// Full REN is "REN" + 11 digits (e.g. REN[REDACTED]). The short 7-digit form
21	// (REN[REDACTED]) hits the POI endpoint but returns an HTML error page, not a PDF.
22	// We require >= 10 digits after the prefix to distinguish the two forms.
23	const FULL_REN_RE = /REN\d{10,}/i;
24	
25	// Try every reasonable extraction path against the raw /api/PolicyId response body.
26	// Returns the full-form REN string, or null if none is found.
27	function extractRen(raw: string): string | null {
28	    // 1. Look for the literal "REN<digits>" pattern directly in the text (covers
29	    //    both JSON string values and any plain-text response body).
30	    const directMatch = raw.match(FULL_REN_RE);
31	    if (directMatch) return directMatch[0].toUpperCase();
32	
33	    // 2. Try JSON parse: look in the most likely field names for a bare numeric id
34	    //    that we can prefix. Carriers sometimes return the id without the "REN" prefix.
35	    try {
36	        const parsed: unknown = JSON.parse(raw);
37	        if (parsed && typeof parsed === "object") {
38	            const obj = parsed as Record<string, unknown>;
39	            for (const key of ["PolicyId", "policyId", "policyNumber", "id", "Id", "renNumber"]) {
40	                const val = obj[key];
41	                if (typeof val === "string") {
42	                    // Could be "REN[REDACTED]" or "66501720005" (bare digits)
43	                    const withPrefix = /^REN/i.test(val) ? val.toUpperCase() : `REN${val}`;
44	                    if (FULL_REN_RE.test(withPrefix)) return withPrefix;
45	                }
46	                if (typeof val === "number") {
47	                    const withPrefix = `REN${val}`;
48	                    if (FULL_REN_RE.test(withPrefix)) return withPrefix;
49	                }
50	            }
51	        }
52	    } catch {
53	        // not JSON — fall through to regex pass on raw text
54	    }
55	
56	    // 3. Regex pass: find a bare-digit run of the accepted full-REN length anywhere
57	    //    and prefix it. Matched length (>= 10) is aligned with FULL_REN_RE so any
58	    //    bare run the validator would accept is also caught here.
59	    const bareMatch = raw.match(/\b(\d{10,})\b/);
60	    if (bareMatch) {
61	        const candidate = `REN${bareMatch[1]}`;
62	        if (FULL_REN_RE.test(candidate)) return candidate;
63	    }
64	
65	    return null;
66	}
67	
68	// Real Assurant (renters) portal automation. Auth is an embedded Okta widget:
69	// inputs #okta-signin-username / #okta-signin-password, submit #okta-signin-submit.
70	// MFA is an Okta SMS code into input[name=answer]. After login the account lands
71	// on /app/policy/selection; documents live on the server-rendered /Policy/Documents.
72	// Shared Browserbase plumbing (session + downloads) lives in BrowserbaseSession.
73	export class AssurantCarrier implements Carrier {
74	    readonly name = "assurant";
75	    private session?: BrowserbaseSession;
76	
77	    // Open the browser and load the Okta login form. No credentials needed, so
78	    // this can run ahead of
… [truncated 13792 chars]

22	// We intercept BrowserbaseSession.prototype.fetchInPage to capture the raw
23	// /api/PolicyId response body ONCE, purely diagnostically (the carrier's call
24	// flow is unchanged; we only peek at the return value). The patch is applied
25	// inside the try below and always restored in finally, so a throw during setup
26	// can never leave the prototype monkey-patched.
27	const _origFn = BrowserbaseSession.prototype.fetchInPage;
28	// Holder object so the closure's assignment is visible to the type checker (a
29	// captured `let` gets narrowed to null since TS can't see the closure mutate it).
30	const capture: { body: string | null } = { body: null };
31	let patched = false;
32	
33	const c = new AssurantCarrier();
34	try {
35	    // Apply the diagnostic patch. Paired with the restore in finally.
36	    BrowserbaseSession.prototype.fetchInPage = async function (
37	        this: BrowserbaseSession,
38	        url: string,
39	        opts?: { method?: string; headers?: Record<string, string>; body?: string },
40	    ) {
41	        const result = await _origFn.call(this, url, opts ?? {});
42	        if (/\/api\/PolicyId/i.test(url) && capture.body === null) {
43	            capture.body = Buffer.from(result.base64, "base64").toString("utf8");
44	        }
45	        return result;
46	    };
47	    patched = true;
48	
49	    const tPrep = Date.now();
50	    await c.prepare();
51	    console.log(`[phase] prepare(): ${Date.now() - tPrep}ms  (pre-warm, off the graded clock)`);
52	
53	    const tLogin = Date.now();
54	    const { mfaRequired } = await c.login(process.env.ASSURANT_USER!, process.env.ASSURANT_PASSWORD!);
55	    console.log(`[phase] login(): ${Date.now() - tLogin}ms  (mfaRequired: ${mfaRequired})`);
56	
57	    let code = "";
58	    if (mfaRequired) {
59	        console.log(">>> drop SMS code into scripts/assurant-mfa.txt");
60	        for (let i = 0; i < 150; i++) {

Backend automation runs on Fly/\n// Browserbase exactly as a real user would hit it; this is just the client UI.\n//   ! node --env-file=.env --import tsx scripts/prod-ui-drive.ts\nimport { chromium } from \"playwright\";\nimport { existsSync, readFileSync, rmSync } from \"node:fs\";\n\nconst URL = process.env.PROD_URL ?? \"https://take-home-policy-puller.fly.dev\";\n\nconst browser = await chromium.launch({ headless: false });\nconst page = await browser.newPage();\ntry {\n  console.log(`opening ${URL} ...`);\n  await page.goto(URL, { waitUntil: \"domcontentloaded\" });\n\n  // page-load fires /prepare (pre-warm) on its own; pick Assurant + fill creds\n  await page.locator(\"#carrier\").waitFor({ timeout: 30_000 });\n  await page.selectOption(\"#carrier\", \"assurant\");\n  await page.fill(\"#username\", process.env.ASSURANT_USER ?? \"\");\n  await page.fill(\"#password\", process.env.ASSURANT_PASSWORD ?? \"\");\n\n  // give the pre-warm a moment so the click reuses the warm session\n  await page.waitForTimeout(1500);\n  console.log(\"submitting login ...\");\n  await page.click(\"#login-btn\");\n\n  // wait for either the MFA field or a final render (trusted-device skip)\n  const mfa = page.locator(\"#code\");\n  const docs = page.locator(\"#docs-section iframe\");\n  const outcome = await Promise.race([\n    mfa.waitFor({ state: \"visible\", timeout: 60_000 }).then(() => \"mfa\" as const),\n    docs.waitFor({ state: \"visible\", timeout: 60_000 }).then(() => \"done\" as const),\n  ]).catch(() => \"neither\" as const);\n\n  let tGradedStart = 0;\n  if (outcome === \"mfa\") {\n    console.log(\">>> MFA field is up. Drop the SMS code into scripts/assurant-mfa.txt\");\n    let code = \"\";\n    for (let i = 0; i < 150; i++) {\n      if (existsSync(\"scripts/assurant-mfa.txt\")) {\n        code = readFileSync(\"scripts/assurant-mfa.txt\", \"utf8\").trim();\n        rmSync(\"scripts/assurant-mfa.txt\");\n        break;\n      }\n      await new Promise((r) => setTimeout(r, 2000));\n    }\n    if (!code) throw new Error(\"no code received in time\");\n    await page.fill(\"#code\", code);\n    // GRADED clock: the instant we submit the code, matching the frontend's mfaAt\n    tGradedStart = Date.now();\n    await page.click(\"#mfa-btn\");\n  } else if (outcome === \"done\") {\n    console.log(\"trusted device: no MFA, login went straight to documents\");\n  } else {\n    throw new Error(\"neither MFA field nor documents appeared within 60s\");\n  }\n\n  // wait for the document to actually render in the page\n  await docs.waitFor({ state: \"visible\", timeout: 60_000 });\n  const ourGraded = tGradedStart ? Date.now() - tGradedStart : null;\n\n  // read the number the FRONTEND itself computed and shows in its status line\n  const status = (await page.locator(\"#status\").innerText().catch(() => \"\")).trim();\n\n  console.log(\"\\n===== PROD UI RESULT =====\");\n  if (ourGraded !== null) console.log(`our stopwatch (MFA submit -> iframe visible): ${(ourGraded / 1000).toFixed(2)}s`);\n  console.log(`frontend status line: ${status}`);\n  // count rendered docs\n  const n = await page.locator(\"#docs-section iframe\").count();\n  console.log(`documents rendered: ${n}`);\n  console.log(\"\\nleaving the window open 8s so you can see it ...\");\n  await page.waitForTimeout(8000);\n} catch (e) {\n  console.log(\"ERROR:\", (e as Error).message);\n} finally {\n  await browser.close();\n}\nprocess.exit(0);\n"}

## What the prod UI run proved (you did the MFA in the real browser)

The fast path executed end to end on prod, from the server `[timing]` logs:
- `policyid: 316ms (status=200)` → **`/api/PolicyId` returns the full REN, and the parser extracted it.** This was the whole unknown. It works.
- `poi: 2704ms (status=200, application/pdf)` → **POI returns the COC PDF directly.** No nav-docs, no download clicks, no poll.
- `GRADED mfa-submit→docs: 10786ms`

So the approach is validated live. The PDF rendered. The only problem is the number.

## Why it's 10.8s and not ~6s

Decomposing the 10,786ms:

| Piece | Time | Note |
|---|---|---|
| `submitMfa` (Okta verify + redirect) | 3,484 ms | carrier-side, fixed |
| **anti-bot hardening** (2× `networkidle` settles + activate nav + 2× jitter) | **~4,282 ms** | the reviewers' caution, and the killer |
| `policyid` | 316 ms | real work |
| `poi` | 2,704 ms | real work |

The actual useful work is only ~3.0s. **~4.3s is pure hardening overhead** the reviewers added (the `networkidle` waits never settle fast because the SPA keeps firing XHRs). For a one-user, low-volume demo that's massively over-cautious.

## The fix (clear, low-risk)
Cut the two `networkidle` settles and the jitters, keep the cheap activate nav:
- Projected: `submitMfa 3.5 + activate ~0.7 + policyid 0.3 + poi 2.7 ≈ **7.2s**` → under 8s.
- Make the activate nav conditional (try POI from `/selection` first) → **~6.5s**.

Honest caveat: the carrier floor is `submitMfa 3.5 + poi 2.7 ≈ 6.2s`, and both vary run to run, so it'll clear 8s but not by a mile.

Want me to apply the trim, redeploy, and do one more UI run to confirm we're under 8s?

Diagnostic is conclusive. Here's exactly what's happening.

## This account has 2 documents, and we've only been returning 1

| Document | Size | UI control | How it's fetched |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Declarations Page** (the real policy doc) | ~511 KB | `<a>` labeled **"Declarations Page"** | `GET /api/Policies/{REN}/Document?documentToken=[REDACTED]&lob=RI` |
| **Confirmation of Coverage** (proof of coverage) | 58 KB | `<button>` labeled **"Download"** | `GET /api/v2/Policies/{REN}/POI/ConfirmationOfCoverage?outputMode=file` |

**Why only the COC ever showed:**
- The **download path** matches controls by the text `/download/i`. The COC button says "Download" so it matched. The Declarations Page link says "Declarations Page", not "Download", so it was **silently skipped**.
- The **fast path** only ever fetches the COC POI endpoint and never looks at the documents list.

So the Declarations Page (the actual policy you were looking for) has been missed by both.

## The catch for fetching it fast
The Declarations Page needs a `documentToken` (an opaque, per-session encrypted string). The probe confirmed:
- Fetching by document `Id` **fails** (500 / threw on every pattern).
- The token is **not** a field in the documents-list JSON (I checked the full field list — no token field).
- The token only exists on the **rendered documents-page anchor**, which the Angular app mints client-side.

That means to get the Declarations Page, we have to **render the documents page** (`nav-docs`, ~5.5s) to scrape the token. There's no cheap API shortcut for it like there was for the COC.

## So this is a real fork: completeness vs sub-8s
- **Complete** (both docs): requires `nav-docs`, so Assurant lands ~10-12s, over the 8s target.
- **Fast** (current): COC only, ~7-8s, but missing the actual policy document.

The prompt says "App pulls the policy documents," and you flagged the gap, so I lean toward completeness with the latency documented as an honest tradeoff (Allstate already carries the sub-8s story). But it's your call.

assistant
**Cracked it.** The token needs no crypto — the Angular source (`dlc.js`, `DocumentsListComponentController`) builds the href literally as:

```js
return App.serverEndpoint + apiUrl + "?documentToken=" + encodeURIComponent(document.DocId) + "&lob=" + LOB;
```

**`documentToken` = `encodeURIComponent(DocId)`**, and `DocId` is a field on each item in the Documents list JSON. The opaque `[REDACTED_TOKEN] token I saw is just the URL-encoded `DocId` value. My earlier "token isn't in the list" call was wrong — the probe truncated the doc object before the `DocId` field (it's the last field in the key list).

So **fast AND complete is achievable, no page render needed:**
1. `/api/PolicyId` → full REN (~0.3s)
2. `/api/Policies/{REN}/Documents?lob=RI` → list, each item has `DocId` (~0.5s)
3. Per doc: `/api/Policies/{REN}/Document?documentToken=[REDACTED]&lob=RI` (in-page) — the Declarations Page
4. `/api/v2/Policies/{REN}/POI/ConfirmationOfCoverage?outputMode=file` — the COC
5. Fire 3+4 in parallel → gated by the slowest (~2.7s)

Projected: `submitMfa 3.5 + REN 0.3 + list 0.5 + parallel-fetch ~2.7 ≈ ~7s`, **under 8s and complete** — once I also strip the ~4.3s of networkidle hardening that bloated the last run.

I'll implement this via a workflow (implement + anti-bot/correctness review), writing to scratch so the working tree is untouched until vetted. It also fixes the fallback selector to catch the "Declarations Page" anchor so even the fallback is complete.

You made the right call. Leaving git alone is the safe move, and nothing is lost:
- The other agent's work (`da8bf16` + the 7 uncommitted files) is sitting intact in the working tree.
- My fast-path code is isolated in `/tmp` scratch and the workflow keeps writing there, so it isn't touching the repo at all.
- Your earlier backups (`assurant-working-baseline`, `backup-assurant-fastpath`) are safe on GitHub.

The actual problem is simple to name: **two agents are sharing one folder and one git checkout.** That's the hazard. Whoever switches branches or rebases yanks the floor out from under the other. Nothing is corrupted right now, it's just fragile.

The clean way to handle it safely, in plain terms:

1. **One folder, one agent.** The simplest rule: don't have two agents editing the same directory at once. Right now the other agent "owns" this folder (it's on their `stream-docs` branch with live edits), so I should not modify files here until they finish and commit.

2. **Or give each agent its own folder (git worktree).** This is the proper fix. `git worktree` makes a second working directory on its own branch that shares the same repo history. The other agent keeps this folder; I get my own. They can't collide. Important: creating a worktree does **not** touch this folder or their uncommitted work, so it respects "leave git alone" here.

What I recommend, and what I'll do unless you say otherwise:
- I leave this shared tree completely alone (no checkout, rebase, stash, or edits to `src/`).
- I let the fast-path workflow finish writing the vetted code to `/tmp` so it's ready.
- I **don't apply or deploy** it into this tree while the other agent has uncommitted work.

Then, when you're ready, pick one:
- **Wait**: let the other agent commit + push `stream-docs`, then I apply my fastpath cleanly on top.
- **Worktree**: I set up a separate folder for my fastpath (off `origin/main`), apply + test + commit there, fully isolated from `stream-docs`. I'll walk you through it and it won't touch this folder.

No rush, and nothing breaks by waiting. Which do you prefer?

## What `fetchDocuments` does now
**Complete + fast + streaming**, reconciled with the merged streaming contract:

1. `fetchDocuments(onDoc?)` — accepts the streaming callback.
2. **REN** via `/api/PolicyId` (in-page), with conditional activate (only clicks to `/snapshot` if the first call yields no REN). No `networkidle` waits.
3. **Documents list** via `/api/Policies/{REN}/Documents?lob=RI` → `DocId` per item.
4. **Parallel in-page fetch**: each listed doc via `documentToken=[REDACTED] **+** the COC via the POI endpoint, staggered to avoid a same-millisecond burst.
5. As each PDF's bytes land → `onDoc?.(doc)` (streams immediately, like Allstate), then returns the full set.
6. **Fallback** (nav-docs download) now catches the "Declarations Page" anchor too (`a[href*="documentToken"]` + declaration/coverage link text), so even the slow path is complete. It also streams via `onDoc`.

So for your account it should return **both**: the Declarations Page (~511 KB) and the Confirmation of Coverage (~58 KB), each painting as it arrives.

assistant
Good instinct, and you're probably right. Here's the honest distinction:

- **Declarations Page** (`REN-6650172-00`, DocumentType "Declaration Page/New/Renewal") — this is the **actual policy document**. It lives in the official documents list (`/api/Policies/{REN}/Documents`). This is unambiguously what "policy documents" means.
- **Confirmation of Coverage** — a **proof-of-coverage letter**, generated on demand via a separate endpoint (`/POI/ConfirmationOfCoverage`). It's **not in the documents list** at all. It's the thing you'd send a landlord as proof of insurance, not the policy itself.

So scoping to "the documents list" (Declarations Page) is the cleaner, more defensible reading of "pull the policy documents." The COC is arguably a bonus, not a requirement.

Two caveats so you decide with full info:
1. The COC is the **always-available** one. The Declarations Page depends on the list having items (a brand-new policy mid-processing might show only the COC). For your account both exist, so this is only a robustness footnote.
2. **Latency:** dropping the COC removes one parallel fetch (~1s), but it's not the magic bullet for sub-8s. This run's 9.6s was dominated by the **activate + PolicyId retry (~2.2s)** and the **511 KB Declarations Page over CDP (~the 4s parallel batch)**. Drop the COC and you're likely ~8.5s, still a hair over 8.

My recommendation: scope it to the **documents list (Declarations Page)** and drop the COC, since that's the literal "policy documents." Want me to make that change? (It also lets me drop the COC's stagger slot and simplify the parallel step.) I won't touch anything until you confirm.

# Writing git commit messages

Default: one short subject line. State exactly what was done. Nothing else.

Add a body only when the WHY is non-obvious from the diff, and keep it to 1 or 2 terse lines. KISS.

Source: https://cbea.ms/git-commit/

## The seven rules

1. Separate subject from body with a blank line.
2. Limit subject to 50 chars (72 is the hard ceiling).
3. Capitalize the subject (override below for repo-specific prefix style).
4. No period at the end of the subject.
5. Imperative mood. "Fix bug" not "Fixed bug" or "Fixes bug".
6. Wrap the body at 72 chars.
7. Body explains what and why, not how. The diff already shows how.

## The subject-line test

A good subject completes the sentence: "If applied, this commit will ___."

Passes: "Refactor X module". Fails: "Fixed bug", "Sweeping changes", "More fixes".

## Style rules (hard)

- No em dashes or en dashes anywhere. Use periods, commas, or restructure.
- No semicolons. Comma or period.
- No emojis.
- No `Co-Authored-By:` lines.
- No `Generated with Claude Code` or similar footers.
- Never list Claude as author. Check `git config user.name` and `user.email` before committing.
- Don't repeat the prefix in the description. `fix: Fix X` is redundant.

## Plain verbs to default to

fix, add, remove, rename, move, extract, drop, revert, bump, pin, unpin, wire up, clean up, stub out, expose, hide, replace, restore, ignore, gate, skip.

## Banned AI-tell words

comprehensive, enhance, streamline, robust, leverage, utilize, ensure, rectify, "this commit introduces", "implement comprehensive", "this change adds support for".

If any appear in a draft, rewrite the subject.

## Repo-specific overrides

If the repo's `AGENTS.md` or `CONTRIBUTING.md` defines a style, follow that instead of rule 3:

- **Peeky style**: lowercase area prefix, colon, terse description. Examples: `tuning: zero post-release grace`, `demos: move examples/ to demos/`, `deny: ignore RUSTSEC-2026-0009`.
- **Conventional Commits style**: `feat(scope): ...`, `fix(scope): ...`, `chore(scope): ...` (used in Node/Angular/Vercel ecosystems).

The other six rules still apply.

## When a body is justified

- The change is non-obvious from the diff (workaround, perf trick, surprising ordering).
- The why needs context outside this file (incident ID, advisory, upstream bug).
- Closing a tracked issue: include `closes #N` (repeat per issue, a shared keyword only closes the first).

If the diff explains itself, write no body. One line is enough.

## Examples

Good, single-line:

```
tuning: zero post-release grace
demos: move examples/ to demos/
deny: ignore RUSTSEC-2026-0009 (time, blocked by tract pin)
fix rustfmt on screenshot guard in find_action
```

Good, with justified body:

```
routelet: cap the opt-in log and document data handling

Bound routelet_log.jsonl to its last 5000 lines. Storage cap, not a
privacy fix. Logging is already opt-in and redacted.
```

Bad (rewrite these):

```
Add comprehensive support for enhanced cursor positioning
```
Rewrite as: `cursor: snap to nearest target on partial match`.

```
This commit introduces a robust solution for the STT cutoff issue
```
Rewrite as: `stt: add 200ms post-release grace to capture trailing audio`.

## Workflow

1. Stage exact paths. Never `git add -A` or `git add .`.
2. `git status` to confirm only your changes are staged.
3. Draft the subject. Apply the "If applied" test.
4. Body only if justified above.
5. `git commit -m "..."` with HEREDOC for multi-line.
6. Never push unless asked.

## Red flags

- Subject describes how, not what or why.
- Subject would still make sense if pasted into a different PR. Too vague.
- Body restates the diff line by line.
- Two unrelated changes in one commit. Split them.
- Any banned word above.

For deeper coverage, see the `writing` skill (manual invoke: `/writing`) which compiles all writing rules, or `d

tool result
1	# Policy Puller
2	
3	Pulls a user's insurance policy PDFs from carrier portals by automating a cloud
4	browser. Pick a carrier, enter credentials, pass MFA, get the documents.
5	
6	Live: https://take-home-policy-puller.fly.dev/
7	
8	## Carriers
9	
10	- **Allstate** (custom login + SMS MFA, documents from the portal's JSON API)
11	- **Geico** renters (Okta login + SMS MFA, serviced via Assurant's portal)
12	
13	Both implement one `Carrier` interface, so a third is one file.
14	
15	## Run
16	
17	```sh
18	npm install        # .env needs BROWSERBASE_API_KEY and BROWSERBASE_PROJECT_ID
19	npm run dev        # http://localhost:3000
20	npm test           # mock-driven endpoint tests, no Browserbase
21	fly deploy         # one long-running machine in iad
22	```
23	
24	## How it works
25	
26	Long-running Express backend, because it holds the browser across the MFA pause
27	(not serverless). The browser runs on Browserbase with a residential proxy, off your
28	machine. Session state is an in-memory Map. One static HTML page, no build step.
29	
30	Flow: `/prepare` opens the browser on page load (pre-warm), `/login` submits
31	credentials, if MFA the UI shows a code field, `/mfa` submits it, documents render.
32	
33	## Anti-bot
34	
35	What matters is egress (the IP the carrier sees), not compute (where the browser runs).
36	A datacenter IP is flagged on sight, which is why local Playwright works but a VM does
37	not. So the browser runs on Browserbase with a residential proxy and a Verified
38	fingerprint.
39	
40	Allstate runs Akamai plus F5. With the residential proxy, Verified, and real input,
41	Akamai's `_abck` validates to status 0, so the session passes the sensor instead of
42	riding unenforced endpoints. Documents then come from the portal's JSON API. The
43	per-carrier tradeoff and the probe evidence are in [`latency.md`](latency.md).
44	
45	## Latency
46	
47	Measured on prod. The brief grades MFA submission to document on screen, which on a
48	trusted device is the document fetch:
49	
50	- Graded fetch: **~6 to 8s**
51	- Repeat run (session reuse): **~3s**
52	- Full login-click to on screen: ~10 to 13s, including the ~4s login that cannot be pre-warmed
53	
54	The login page is pre-warmed on page load so it overlaps typing, and the UI shows the
55	graded span on screen.
56	
57	## Session reuse
58	
59	After a successful run the validated browser is kept alive, keyed by
60	`sha256(carrier, username, password)`. A repeat login with the same credentials
61	refetches on the live session and skips login. The key is a hash, so a wrong password
62	cannot reach another session and no credential is stored.
63	
64	## Limitations
65	
66	- A single cold login against a live anti-bot portal is not 100% reliable; under heavy
67	  velocity the carrier slow-walks the login. Reuse means that fragile step runs once per
68	  session window, not every time.
69	- No per-operation timeout yet, so a hung login surfaces slowly.
70	- Login success is read from the page, not an API, and is bespoke per carrier. See
71	  [`assumptions.md`](assumptions.md).
72

<h1>Claude session: export7</h1>
<div class="msg user text"><div class="label">user</div><pre>ok so lets zoom in on the full api. but lets just talk about it right now, what is our current implementation ?</pre></div>
<div class="msg assistant text"><div class="label">assistant</div><pre>Right now `main` does NOT use the full API. `main`'s Allstate `fetchDocuments` is pure UI nav: click Policies dropdown, click "Documents for ... policy", read the table anchors, click each title to trigger a popup+download, then pull bytes from Browserbase's download storage. That's the ~12s path.

The full-API version only exists on the branch `allstate-api-experiment` (not merged). And honestly what we have committed there is the *recipe proven out*, plus the discovery script (`scripts/allstate-docsniff.ts`). Let me lay out the full-API flow as it stands:

**The 4 calls (all via `page.request`, in-browser, authed by session cookies):**

1. `GET /api/secured/GetUserData` → grab `policies[0].policyImage.number` (the policy number).
2. `GET /api/secured/document/GetDocumentsForPolicies` → the **context primer**. Returns an empty body, but without it step 3 comes back empty. This was the blocker we cracked.
3. `POST /api/secured/document/GetPolicySpecificDocsList` with body `{policyNumber, contentId:null, yearFilter}` → `[{title, contentId, docYear}]`, the doc list.
4. `POST /api/secured/document/GetUdpRetrieveDocument` with `{policyNumber, contentId, yearFilter}` per doc → `documentData.{data(base64), mimeType, fileName}`. Fire these in parallel.

**The three things that made it work:**
- CSRF header `x-xsrf-token` must be `decodeURIComponent(XSRF-TOKEN cookie)`, not the raw cookie.
- POST body must be `JSON.stringify(...)`, not a Playwright `data` object (else server sees null body).
- Required headers: `app-name: MYA`, `x-efm: true`, `content-type: application/json` + the decoded token.

// Convert a slice of a Claude Code JSONL transcript to a readable, secret-scrubbed
// HTML export (matches the Infer_notes export-N.html format).
//   node ~/Scripts/export-session.mjs <jsonl> <startLine> <endLine> <outHtml> <title>
import { createReadStream, writeFileSync } from "node:fs";
import { createInterface } from "node:readline";

const [, , file, startStr, endStr, out, title] = process.argv;
const start = Number(startStr), end = Number(endStr);

// ---- secret scrubbing ----
const MFA = ["[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]", "[MFA]"];
function scrub(s) {
  if (!s) return s;
  let o = s;
  o = o.replace(/[REDACTED_PW]/g, "[REDACTED_PW]");
  o = o.replace(/\b97913\b/g, "[REDACTED]");
  o = o.replace(/bb_live_[A-Za-z0-9]+/g, "bb_live_[REDACTED]");
  o = o.replace(new RegExp(`\\b(${MFA.join("|")})\\b`, "g"), "[MFA]");
  // token/credential fields (json or header style), keep the key
  o = o.replace(/("?(passCode|answer|password|pwd|sessionToken|stateToken|access_token|id_token|deviceToken|authorization|x-xsrf-token|xsrf-token|cookie)"?\s*[:=]\s*\\?"?)[^"&,}\s\\]+/gi, "$1[REDACTED]");
  o = o.replace(/Bearer\s+[A-Za-z0-9._-]+/g, "Bearer [REDACTED]");
  o = o.replace(/REN\d{6,}/g, "REN[REDACTED]");
  o = o.replace(/\b[REDACTED_POLICY]\b/g, "[REDACTED_POLICY]");
  o = o.replace(/82 Tern L(ane|n)/gi, "[REDACTED_ADDR]");
  o = o.replace(/[REDACTED_CITY]/g, "[REDACTED_CITY]");
  return o;
}
const esc = (s) => scrub(String(s ?? "")).replace(/&/g, "&amp;").replace(/</g, "&lt;").replace(/>/g, "&gt;");
const trunc = (s, n = 4000) => (s.length > n ? s.slice(0, n) + `\n… [truncated ${s.length - n} chars]` : s);

function renderContent(role, content, parts) {
  if (typeof content === "string") {
    let t = content.replace(/<system-reminder>[\s\S]*?<\/system-reminder>/g, "[system-reminder omitted]");
